# sei.creation_traces - Dune Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/sei/raw/creation-traces#content-area)

[Dune Docs home page![light logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo/logo/dune-logo-light.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo&q=85&s=8344ffbb623f6875145727e13925a620)![dark logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo/logo/dune-logo-dark.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo&q=85&s=54f1a9a73ae8fe5ec0235a2e52f9b870)](https://dune.com/)

Search...

⌘KAsk AI

Search...

Navigation

Raw (EVM)

sei.creation\_traces

[Docs](https://docs.dune.com/home)
[Data Catalog](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/overview)
[API Reference](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction)
[SQL Query Engine](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/overview)
[Resources](https://docs.dune.com/resources/credits-billing/overview)

Table Description
-----------------

The `sei.creation_traces` table contains information about the creation of smart contracts on the sei blockchain. This includes the address of the contract, the address of the creator, the block number at which the contract was created, the transaction hash, and the contract's bytecode. This table is useful for understanding the deployment of smart contracts on the sei blockchain.

This table is a subset of the `traces` table, which contains information about all traces on the sei blockchain. The `creation_traces` table is filtered to only include traces that create new smart contracts. The filter for this is `type = 'create'` .

Column Descriptions
-------------------

Datatypes on Snowflake datashare are different in some cases, read more [here](https://docs.dune.com/datashare/datashare#datatypes)
.

Table Sample
------------

Examples
--------

### Show the creation of a specific smart contract

    SELECT * FROM sei.creation_traces
    WHERE contract_address = 0x06012c8cf97bead5deae237070f9587f8e7a266d

### Show the creation of smart contracts by a specific creator

    SELECT * FROM sei.creation_traces
    WHERE "from" = 0x0d4a11d5eeaac28ec3f61d100da81f6a1b65c9d6

### Show the creation of smart contracts in the last 10 days

    SELECT 
        date_trunc('day', block_time) AS day,
        COUNT(*)
    FROM sei.creation_traces
    GROUP BY 1
    ORDER BY 1 DESC
    LIMIT 10

# sei.traces - Dune Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/sei/raw/traces#content-area)

[Dune Docs home page![light logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo/logo/dune-logo-light.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo&q=85&s=8344ffbb623f6875145727e13925a620)![dark logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo/logo/dune-logo-dark.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo&q=85&s=54f1a9a73ae8fe5ec0235a2e52f9b870)](https://dune.com/)

Raw (EVM)

sei.traces

[Docs](https://docs.dune.com/home)
[Data Catalog](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/overview)
[API Reference](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction)
[SQL Query Engine](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/overview)
[Resources](https://docs.dune.com/resources/credits-billing/overview)

Table Description
-----------------

The `sei.traces` table contains the traces of the transactions executed on the Ethereum Virtual Machine (EVM). It includes the traces of the transaction and the traces of the internal transactions. Traces are the result of the execution of the transaction and are used to debug and understand the execution of the transaction. They are also known as \`internal transactions\` and can be used to understand the execution of a transaction.

This is the raw version of this table. If the chain is a Fully Managed chain, decoded transaction calls will be available, see [call tables](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/sei/decoded/call-tables)
 section. If this is a Hosted chain, decoded call tables will not be available.

Column Descriptions
-------------------

Datatypes on Snowflake datashare are different in some cases, read more [here](https://docs.dune.com/datashare/datashare#datatypes)
.

Table Sample
------------

Example
-------

### Querying traces for a specific transaction hash

    SELECT *
    FROM sei.traces
    WHERE tx_hash = 0xb30d6d67cf7d148c2257bf598c5f5cdf5912a3d05c7d3b000398d675d2fa912c

# Shape Overview - Dune Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/shape/overview#content-area)

[Dune Docs home page![light logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo/logo/dune-logo-light.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo&q=85&s=8344ffbb623f6875145727e13925a620)![dark logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo/logo/dune-logo-dark.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo&q=85&s=54f1a9a73ae8fe5ec0235a2e52f9b870)](https://dune.com/)

Search...

⌘KAsk AI

Search...

Navigation

Shape

Shape Overview

[Docs](https://docs.dune.com/home)
[Data Catalog](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/overview)
[API Reference](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction)
[SQL Query Engine](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/overview)
[Resources](https://docs.dune.com/resources/credits-billing/overview)

On this page

*   [Data Catalog](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/shape/overview#data-catalog)
    

Shape is the chain for creators, built on top of Ethereum. It is an EVM equivalent Layer 2 scaling solution that inherits its security directly from Ethereum, keeping the networks intrinsically linked forever. **Chain for Creators with Gasback:** As a creator on Shape, you can claim back 80% of sequencer fees users spend interacting with your contracts. This includes contracts you build yourself, contracts you acquire ownership of, and contracts that you deploy through other platforms. **EVM Equivalent:** Shape is fully EVM equivalent, providing the same creator experience as on Ethereum, just at a fraction of the cost. This enables developers to deploy existing smart contracts and dApps without the need for extensive modifications. **Secure, Stable & Scalable:** Shape inherits its security directly from Ethereum and prioritizes stability and scalability, utilizing Alchemy and Optimism as key infrastructure partners to help achieve and maintain these states. **Part of the Superchain:** Shape is a member of the Superchain, which unlocks a range of further benefits for the entire ecosystem - including ongoing network-level cooperation, funding of public goods, and additional builder incentives on Shape.

[Shape documentation\
-------------------\
\
Access comprehensive documentation for Shape, providing detailed insights into its technology, platform architecture, and how to build on it.](https://docs.shape.network/documentation/introduction)

[​](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/shape/overview#data-catalog)

Data Catalog
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[Logs\
----\
\
Detailed event logs from smart contracts, offering insights into contract interactions and the dynamics of Shape’s operations.](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/shape/raw/logs)
[Blocks\
------\
\
Information on blocks processed through Shape, illustrating the network’s enhanced throughput and scalability.](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/shape/raw/blocks)
[Transactions\
------------\
\
Extensive transaction data, highlighting the efficiency and reduced costs of operations on Shape.](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/shape/raw/transactions)
[decoded\
-------\
\
Decoded transaction data for easier analysis and deeper understanding of smart contract executions on the Shape network.](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/shape/decoded/overview)

# dex.trades on somnia - Dune Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/somnia/curated-data/dex/dex-trades#content-area)

[Dune Docs home page![light logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo/logo/dune-logo-light.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo&q=85&s=8344ffbb623f6875145727e13925a620)![dark logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo/logo/dune-logo-dark.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo&q=85&s=54f1a9a73ae8fe5ec0235a2e52f9b870)](https://dune.com/)

⌘KAsk AI

Navigation

DEX

dex.trades on somnia

[Docs](https://docs.dune.com/home)
[Data Catalog](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/overview)
[API Reference](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction)
[SQL Query Engine](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/overview)
[Resources](https://docs.dune.com/resources/credits-billing/overview)

This is a cross-chain table but can be filtered for somnia transactions.

Table Description
-----------------

The `dex.trades` table captures detailed data on trades executed via decentralized exchanges (DEXs). This table captures all raw trade events that happen across all liqudity pools. It provides a comprehensive view of the entire trade execution process, detailing the specific paths and liquidity sources utilized.

Functional Overview
-------------------

The `dex.trades` table provides an in-depth view of trades on decentralized exchanges like Uniswap or Curve. This table includes entries for each segment of a trade that passes through different liquidity pools, as well as single-step trades. For example, a user may initiate a trade to swap USDC for PEPE. If this trade is executed through multiple liquidity pools, such as USDC-WETH and WETH-PEPE, the `dex.trades` table will record each segment of the trade as a separate entry. Conversely, a single-step trade, such as directly swapping USDC for ETH, will be recorded as a single entry.This detailed approach allows for granular analysis of trade execution paths, enabling users to:

*   **Analyze Liquidity Sources:** Understand which liquidity pools are used and how they interact in both single-step and multi-step trades.
*   **Track Trade Execution Paths:** Follow the exact route a trade takes across different DEXs and liquidity pools
*   **Assess Slippage and Execution Quality:** Evaluate the impact of each step on the overall trade execution, including slippage and price changes.
*   **Monitor Market Dynamics:** Gain insights into the behavior and dynamics of different liquidity pools and DEXs over time.

Table Coverage
--------------

The following table shows which projects and versions of those projects are covered in the `dex.trades` table on somnia.

Column Descriptions
-------------------

Datatypes on Snowflake datashare are different in some cases, read more [here](https://docs.dune.com/datashare/datashare#datatypes)
.

Table Sample
------------

Navigation

Raw

shape.blocks

[Docs](https://docs.dune.com/home)
[Data Catalog](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/overview)
[API Reference](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction)
[SQL Query Engine](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/overview)
[Resources](https://docs.dune.com/resources/credits-billing/overview)

Table description
-----------------

The `shape.blocks` table contains information about blocks in the shape blockchain. A block is a collection of transactions that are hashed and added to the blockchain. Each block contains a reference to the previous block, known as the parent hash, and a timestamp. The table contains information about each block, such as the block number, the block hash, the block size, the number of transactions, and the gas used.

Column Descriptions
-------------------

Datatypes on Snowflake datashare are different in some cases, read more [here](https://docs.dune.com/datashare/datashare#datatypes)
.

Table Sample
------------

Examples
--------

### Show the most recent blocks

    SELECT
        number,
        hash, 
        size,
        gas_used
      FROM shape.blocks
      ORDER BY number DESC
      LIMIT 10

### Show the number of blocks mined each day

    SELECT
        date_trunc('day', time) AS day,
        count(distinct number)
      FROM shape.blocks
      GROUP BY day
      ORDER BY day DESC

### Show the number of transactions in each block

    SELECT
        number,
        count(*)
      FROM shape.blocks
      GROUP BY 1 
      LIMIT 10

Was this page helpful?

YesNo

# shape.transactions - Dune Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/shape/raw/transactions#content-area)

[Dune Docs home page![light logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo/logo/dune-logo-light.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo&q=85&s=8344ffbb623f6875145727e13925a620)![dark logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo/logo/dune-logo-dark.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo&q=85&s=54f1a9a73ae8fe5ec0235a2e52f9b870)](https://dune.com/)

⌘KAsk AI

Search...

Navigation

Raw

shape.transactions

[Docs](https://docs.dune.com/home)
[Data Catalog](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/overview)
[API Reference](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction)
[SQL Query Engine](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/overview)
[Resources](https://docs.dune.com/resources/credits-billing/overview)

Table Description
-----------------

The `shape.transactions` table contains information about all transactions on the shape blockchain. Each row represents a single transaction and includes information such as block number, hash, timestamp, sender, recipient, value, gas, gas price, and more. Transactions are the fundamental unit of interaction with the shape blockchain. Transactions are created by users and are used to send value, deploy smart contracts, and interact with smart contracts.

This is the raw version of this table. If the chain is a Fully Managed chain, decoded transaction calls will be available, see [call tables](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/shape/decoded/call-tables)
 section. If this is a Hosted chain, decoded call tables will not be available.

Column Descriptions
-------------------

Datatypes on Snowflake datashare are different in some cases, read more [here](https://docs.dune.com/datashare/datashare#datatypes)
.

Table Sample
------------

Examples
--------

### Show all transactions sent by a specific address

    SELECT * 
    FROM shape.transactions WHERE "from" = '0x50A1b5c358F8D34F0d35aA2f10742c46054E247e'
    

### Count the number of transactions per block

    SELECT 
        block_number, 
        COUNT(*)
    FROM shape.transactions
    GROUP BY 1
    ORDER BY 1 DESC
    LIMIT 10
    

### Show the top 10 transactions with the highest gas price

    SELECT 
        hash, 
        gas_price
    FROM shape.transactions
    ORDER BY gas_price DESC
    LIMIT 10

# shape.traces - Dune Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/shape/raw/traces#content-area)

[Dune Docs home page![light logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo/logo/dune-logo-light.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo&q=85&s=8344ffbb623f6875145727e13925a620)![dark logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo/logo/dune-logo-dark.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo&q=85&s=54f1a9a73ae8fe5ec0235a2e52f9b870)](https://dune.com/)

Raw

shape.traces

[Docs](https://docs.dune.com/home)
[Data Catalog](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/overview)
[API Reference](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction)
[SQL Query Engine](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/overview)
[Resources](https://docs.dune.com/resources/credits-billing/overview)

Table Description
-----------------

The `shape.traces` table contains the traces of the transactions executed on the Ethereum Virtual Machine (EVM). It includes the traces of the transaction and the traces of the internal transactions. Traces are the result of the execution of the transaction and are used to debug and understand the execution of the transaction. They are also known as \`internal transactions\` and can be used to understand the execution of a transaction.

This is the raw version of this table. If the chain is a Fully Managed chain, decoded transaction calls will be available, see [call tables](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/shape/decoded/call-tables)
 section. If this is a Hosted chain, decoded call tables will not be available.

Column Descriptions
-------------------

Datatypes on Snowflake datashare are different in some cases, read more [here](https://docs.dune.com/datashare/datashare#datatypes)
.

Table Sample
------------

Example
-------

### Querying traces for a specific transaction hash

    SELECT *
    FROM shape.traces
    WHERE tx_hash = 0xb30d6d67cf7d148c2257bf598c5f5cdf5912a3d05c7d3b000398d675d2fa912c

# Somnia Call Tables - Dune Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/somnia/decoded/call-tables#content-area)

[Dune Docs home page![light logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo/logo/dune-logo-light.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo&q=85&s=8344ffbb623f6875145727e13925a620)![dark logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo/logo/dune-logo-dark.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo&q=85&s=54f1a9a73ae8fe5ec0235a2e52f9b870)](https://dune.com/)

⌘KAsk AI

Navigation

Decoded

Somnia Call Tables

[Docs](https://docs.dune.com/home)
[Data Catalog](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/overview)
[API Reference](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction)
[SQL Query Engine](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/overview)
[Resources](https://docs.dune.com/resources/credits-billing/overview)

On this page

*   [Overview](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/somnia/decoded/call-tables#overview)
    
*   [Decoding](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/somnia/decoded/call-tables#decoding)
    
*   [Multiple Instances](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/somnia/decoded/call-tables#multiple-instances)
    
*   [Common misconceptions](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/somnia/decoded/call-tables#common-misconceptions)
    
*   [Further Reading](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/somnia/decoded/call-tables#further-reading)
    

[​](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/somnia/decoded/call-tables#overview)

Overview
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

On Dune, we parse all message calls and transactions made to smart contracts in their own tables. This allows us to isolate the logic of a specific smart contract and analyze how it interacts with other smart contracts. The data is stored in the format: `[projectname_blockchain].[contractName]_call_[functionName]` This allows us to analyze how a specific function is used in a smart contract, and how often it is called, as well as how it interacts with other smart contracts. Call tables always originate from the `traces` table, which contains all the transactions and message calls on the Ethereum network. We parse the `data` field of the `traces` table to decode the function call and parameters.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/somnia/decoded/call-tables#decoding)

Decoding
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

When a transaction is sent to a smart contract on the Ethereum network, it contains a `data` field. This `data` field is the encoded function call and parameters. Dune decodes this data and stores it in the corresponding table. For example, when a transaction is sent to the [Uniswap v3 factory](https://etherscan.io/address/0x1f98431c8ad98523631ae4a59f267346ea31f984#code)
 contract on the Ethereum network, Dune will decode the `data` field and store it in the table: `uniswap_v3_ethereum.Factory_call_createPool`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/somnia/decoded/call-tables#multiple-instances)

Multiple Instances
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

For a contract where multiple instances exist, we will decode all calls to all instances of this smart contract into one table. If there are transactions calling the `swap` function of any instance of the [Uniswap v3 pair](https://etherscan.io/address/0x8f8ef111b67c04eb1641f5ff19ee54cda062f163#writeContract)
 contract, we will decode this data into the table `uniswap_v3_ethereum.Pair_call_swap`. The `pair` contract is a template contract and there are many instances of it, each with its own address. The column `contract_address` will indicate the address of the instance of the pair contract that was called.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/somnia/decoded/call-tables#common-misconceptions)

Common misconceptions
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

One thing to keep in mind here is that [web3.js](https://web3js.readthedocs.io/)
, [web3.py](https://web3py.readthedocs.io/en/stable)
 and all other methods of (locally) calling a `pure`, `read`, or `constant` function do not broadcast or publish anything on the blockchain and are therefore not recorded in Dune. However, if one of these functions is invoked by another smart contract in the context of a transaction, this will be broadcast on the chain and therefore accessible in Dune. In short: **State data stored in the memory of a smart contract is not available on Dune!** A good example of this is the function `decimals` of the [erc20 token contract](https://etherscan.io/token/0x1f9840a85d5af5bf1d1762f925bdaddc4201f984#readContract)
 `Uni` which is a `constant` state variable that is able to be accessed through an automatically created “[getter function](https://docs.soliditylang.org/en/v0.7.4/contracts.html#getter-functions)
”. Should a smart contract invoke this function in the context of transaction, this message call will be recorded in the Dune table [`uniswap."UNI_call_decimals"`](https://dune.com/queries/741354)
. This is in contrast to anyone calling this function locally using web3.py/web3.js or using the Etherscan frontend to access this state. These local calls are not recorded in Dune.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/somnia/decoded/call-tables#further-reading)

Further Reading
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[What is the difference between a transaction and a call?\
--------------------------------------------------------](https://ethereum.stackexchange.com/questions/765/what-is-the-difference-between-a-transaction-and-a-call)
[Soliditylang.org documentation\
------------------------------](https://docs.soliditylang.org/en/v0.8.13/contracts.html#function-visibility)
[How Calldata is Encoded\
-----------------------](https://degatchi.com/articles/reading-raw-evm-calldata)

# shape.logs - Dune Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/shape/raw/logs#content-area)

[Dune Docs home page![light logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo/logo/dune-logo-light.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo&q=85&s=8344ffbb623f6875145727e13925a620)![dark logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo/logo/dune-logo-dark.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo&q=85&s=54f1a9a73ae8fe5ec0235a2e52f9b870)](https://dune.com/)

Search...

⌘KAsk AI

Search...

Navigation

Raw

shape.logs

[Docs](https://docs.dune.com/home)
[Data Catalog](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/overview)
[API Reference](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction)
[SQL Query Engine](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/overview)
[Resources](https://docs.dune.com/resources/credits-billing/overview)

Table Description
-----------------

The `shape.logs` table represents the logs generated by the Ethereum Virtual Machine (EVM) when a contract is executed. Logs are a way to store data on the blockchain. Logs originate from events that occur during the execution of a smart contract. A log consists of:

*   topic list: a list of 0 to 3 32-byte data topics. `Topic0` is the hash of the signature of the event (indexed), and the remaining topics are indexed parameters of the event.
*   data: contains non-indexed data.

This is the raw version of this table. If the chain is a Fully Managed chain, decoded transaction calls will be available, see [call tables](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/shape/decoded/call-tables)
 section. If this is a Hosted chain, decoded call tables will not be available.

Column Descriptions
-------------------

Datatypes on Snowflake datashare are different in some cases, read more [here](https://docs.dune.com/datashare/datashare#datatypes)
.

Table Sample
------------

Examples
--------

### Filter the logs for a specific contract

    SELECT *
    FROM shape.logs
    WHERE contract_address = 0x06012c8cf97bead5deae237070f9587f8e7a266d
    LIMIT 10

### Filter the logs for a specific topic

    SELECT *
    FROM shape.logs
    WHERE topic0 = 0xddf252ad1be2c89b69c2b068fc378daa952ba7f163c4a11628f55a4df523b3ef
    

### Show the logs of a specific block

    SELECT *
    FROM shape.logs
    WHERE evt_block_number = 1000000

# Somnia Overview - Dune Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/somnia/overview#content-area)

Somnia

Somnia Overview

[Docs](https://docs.dune.com/home)
[Data Catalog](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/overview)
[API Reference](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction)
[SQL Query Engine](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/overview)
[Resources](https://docs.dune.com/resources/credits-billing/overview)

On this page

*   [What is Somnia?](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/somnia/overview#what-is-somnia)
    
*   [Key Features](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/somnia/overview#key-features)
    
*   [Performance Benchmarks](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/somnia/overview#performance-benchmarks)

*   [Resources](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/somnia/overview#resources)
    

[​](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/somnia/overview#what-is-somnia)

What is Somnia?
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Somnia is a high-performance, cost-efficient EVM-compatible Layer 1 blockchain capable of processing over 1,000,000 transactions per second (TPS) with sub-second finality. It is suitable for serving millions of users and building real-time mass-consumer applications like games, social applications, metaverses, and more, all fully on-chain.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/somnia/overview#key-features)

Key Features
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   **Ultra-High Performance**: Capable of processing over 1,000,000 TPS with sub-second finality
*   **EVM-Compatible**: Full compatibility with Ethereum smart contracts and tooling
*   **Mass-Consumer Focus**: Designed for real-time applications serving millions of users
*   **Cost-Efficient**: Optimized for high-throughput, low-cost transactions
*   **Gaming & Metaverse Ready**: Specialized infrastructure for gaming and metaverse applications
*   **Social Applications**: Built to support large-scale social platforms and applications

[​](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/somnia/overview#performance-benchmarks)

Performance Benchmarks
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   **1,050,000 TPS**: Achieved with ERC-20 transfers between several hundred thousand accounts
*   **50,000 Uniswaps per second**: Running Uniswap V3 with several hundred thousand accounts trading one LP pool
*   **300,000 NFT mints per second**: Supporting 100,000 accounts minting NFTs simultaneously

[​](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/somnia/overview#ecosystem-highlights)

Ecosystem Highlights
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   High-performance infrastructure for mass-consumer applications
*   Gaming and metaverse platform capabilities
*   Social application support at scale
*   Real-time transaction processing
*   Support for various application types including:
    *   Games
    *   Social applications
    *   Metaverses
    *   Real-time consumer applications
    *   High-throughput DeFi protocols

[​](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/somnia/overview#data-on-dune)

Data on Dune
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

--------\
\
Access to raw blockchain data including blocks, transactions, logs, and traces](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/somnia/raw/blocks)
[Decoded Data\
------------\
\
Human-readable contract interactions and events](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/somnia/decoded/overview)

[​](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/somnia/overview#resources)

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------

--------------------\

Official documentation for developers building on Somnia](https://docs.somnia.network/)

# somnia.logs_decoded - Dune Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/somnia/decoded/logs-decoded#content-area)

[Dune Docs home page![light logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo/logo/dune-logo-light.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo&q=85&s=8344ffbb623f6875145727e13925a620)![dark logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo/logo/dune-logo-dark.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo&q=85&s=54f1a9a73ae8fe5ec0235a2e52f9b870)](https://dune.com/)

Decoded

somnia.logs\_decoded

[Docs](https://docs.dune.com/home)
[Data Catalog](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/overview)
[API Reference](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction)
[SQL Query Engine](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/overview)
[Resources](https://docs.dune.com/resources/credits-billing/overview)

Table Description
-----------------

The `logs_decoded` table contains decoded logs from somnia transactions. The table matches `topic0` to the event signature and the corresponding event name. The table does not contain the full event data and is not suitable for analysis of smart contract level data. For that, use the specific event tables as described in [Event Logs](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/somnia/decoded/event-logs)
.This table is great for gaining a high level understanding of the types of events that are being emitted by a smart contract or smart contracts of a certain protocol.

Column Descriptions
-------------------

Datatypes on Snowflake datashare are different in some cases, read more [here](https://docs.dune.com/datashare/datashare#datatypes)
.

Table Sample
------------

# somnia.traces_decoded - Dune Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/somnia/decoded/traces-decoded#content-area)

[Dune Docs home page![light logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo/logo/dune-logo-light.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo&q=85&s=8344ffbb623f6875145727e13925a620)![dark logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo/logo/dune-logo-dark.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo&q=85&s=54f1a9a73ae8fe5ec0235a2e52f9b870)](https://dune.com/)

Decoded

somnia.traces\_decoded

[Docs](https://docs.dune.com/home)
[Data Catalog](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/overview)
[API Reference](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction)
[SQL Query Engine](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/overview)
[Resources](https://docs.dune.com/resources/credits-billing/overview)

Table Description
-----------------

The `traces_decoded` table contains decoded traces from somnia transactions. The table matches `MethodID`, which consists of the first 4 bytes of any eth call, to the trace signature and the corresponding Method name. The table does not contain the full trace data and is not suitable for analysis of smart contract level data. For that, use the specific event tables as described in [Call-tables](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/somnia/decoded/traces-decoded)
.This table is great for gaining a high level understanding of the types of events that are being emitted by a smart contract or smart contracts of a certain protocol.

Column Descriptions
-------------------

Datatypes on Snowflake datashare are different in some cases, read more [here](https://docs.dune.com/datashare/datashare#datatypes)
.

Table Sample
------------

# dex_aggregator.trades on sophon - Dune Docs

[Dune Docs home page![light logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo/logo/dune-logo-light.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo&q=85&s=8344ffbb623f6875145727e13925a620)![dark logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo/logo/dune-logo-dark.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo&q=85&s=54f1a9a73ae8fe5ec0235a2e52f9b870)](https://dune.com/)

DEX

dex\_aggregator.trades on sophon

[Docs](https://docs.dune.com/home)
[Data Catalog](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/overview)
[API Reference](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction)
[SQL Query Engine](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/overview)
[Resources](https://docs.dune.com/resources/credits-billing/overview)

This table is a cross-chain table but can be filtered for sophon transactions.

Table Description
-----------------

The `dex_aggregator.trades` table captures high-level data on trades executed via decentralized exchange (DEX) aggregators. These aggregators aggregate liquidity from multiple DEXs to provide users with the best possible trade execution. Unlike the `dex.trades` table, which records each intermediary step of a trade, `dex_aggregator.trades` condenses the trade data to reflect the user's intended trade, presenting it as a single entry.

Functional Overview
-------------------

Users can expect the `dex_aggregator.trades` table to provide a high-level view of DEX trades facilitated by aggregators. This table simplifies trade records by showing a single entry for trades that may involve multiple DEXs and liquidity pools. For instance, a user might initiate a trade to swap USDC for PEPE via a DEX aggregator. The aggregator might route this trade through several liquidity pools such as WETH-USDC and WETH-PEPE, but `dex_aggregator.trades` will record it as a single USDC → PEPE trade.Complimentary to `dex_aggregator.trades` is the `dex.trades` table, where detailed trade executions are recorded. This table captures the granular steps of each trade, including interactions with different liquidity pools. The volume routed through aggregators is also recorded in the `dex.trades` table. One row in `dex_aggregator.trades` corresponds to one or more rows in `dex.trades`, providing a comprehensive view of the detailed execution path that aggregated trades take.

Coverage
--------

The following table shows which projects and versions of those projects are covered in the `dex.trades` table on sophon.

Column Descriptions
-------------------

Datatypes on Snowflake datashare are different in some cases, read more [here](https://docs.dune.com/datashare/datashare#datatypes)
.

Table Sample
------------

NFT

NFT.trades on sonic

[Docs](https://docs.dune.com/home)
[Data Catalog](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/overview)
[API Reference](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction)
[SQL Query Engine](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/overview)
[Resources](https://docs.dune.com/resources/credits-billing/overview)

This is a cross-chain table but can be filtered for sonic transactions.

Table Description
-----------------

The \`nft.trades\` table on Dune Analytics is central to capturing and analyzing Non-Fungible Token (NFT) transactions across various marketplaces. It is a pivotal resource for dissecting the intricacies of NFT trade execution, market behavior, and collector activity within the NFT space.

Usage
-----

The \`nft.trades\` table serves as an essential tool for delving into the NFT market's complexities. It offers a detailed snapshot of each NFT transaction, encompassing data points such as sale price, transaction timestamp, buyer and seller addresses, and the specific NFT assets involved. This table allows analysts to explore trends in NFT valuation, trading volumes, and marketplace dynamics, providing insights into the evolving landscape of digital collectibles and art.

Table Coverage
--------------

The following table shows which projects and versions of those projects are covered in the `dex.trades` table on sonic.

Column Descriptions
-------------------

Datatypes on Snowflake datashare are different in some cases, read more [here](https://docs.dune.com/datashare/datashare#datatypes)
.

Table Sample

Navigation

DEX

dex.trades on sophon

[Docs](https://docs.dune.com/home)
[Data Catalog](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/overview)
[API Reference](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction)
[SQL Query Engine](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/overview)
[Resources](https://docs.dune.com/resources/credits-billing/overview)

This is a cross-chain table but can be filtered for sophon transactions.

Table Description
-----------------

The `dex.trades` table captures detailed data on trades executed via decentralized exchanges (DEXs). This table captures all raw trade events that happen across all liqudity pools. It provides a comprehensive view of the entire trade execution process, detailing the specific paths and liquidity sources utilized.

Functional Overview
-------------------

The `dex.trades` table provides an in-depth view of trades on decentralized exchanges like Uniswap or Curve. This table includes entries for each segment of a trade that passes through different liquidity pools, as well as single-step trades. For example, a user may initiate a trade to swap USDC for PEPE. If this trade is executed through multiple liquidity pools, such as USDC-WETH and WETH-PEPE, the `dex.trades` table will record each segment of the trade as a separate entry. Conversely, a single-step trade, such as directly swapping USDC for ETH, will be recorded as a single entry.This detailed approach allows for granular analysis of trade execution paths, enabling users to:

*   **Analyze Liquidity Sources:** Understand which liquidity pools are used and how they interact in both single-step and multi-step trades.
*   **Track Trade Execution Paths:** Follow the exact route a trade takes across different DEXs and liquidity pools
*   **Assess Slippage and Execution Quality:** Evaluate the impact of each step on the overall trade execution, including slippage and price changes.
*   **Monitor Market Dynamics:** Gain insights into the behavior and dynamics of different liquidity pools and DEXs over time.

Table Coverage
--------------

The following table shows which projects and versions of those projects are covered in the `dex.trades` table on sophon.

Column Descriptions
-------------------

Datatypes on Snowflake datashare are different in some cases, read more [here](https://docs.dune.com/datashare/datashare#datatypes)
.

Table Sample
------------

# Sonic Overview - Dune Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/sonic/overview#content-area)

[Dune Docs home page![light logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo/logo/dune-logo-light.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo&q=85&s=8344ffbb623f6875145727e13925a620)![dark logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo/logo/dune-logo-dark.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo&q=85&s=54f1a9a73ae8fe5ec0235a2e52f9b870)](https://dune.com/)

Sonic

Sonic Overview

[Docs](https://docs.dune.com/home)
[Data Catalog](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/overview)
[API Reference](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction)
[SQL Query Engine](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/overview)
[Resources](https://docs.dune.com/resources/credits-billing/overview)

On this page

*   [Data Catalog](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/sonic/overview#data-catalog)
    

Sonic is an EVM layer-1 blockchain platform that offers developers attractive incentives and powerful infrastructure, powering the next generation of decentralized applications. The platform features exceptional performance metrics including 10,000 transactions per second and sub-second finality while maintaining full EVM compatibility. **High Scalability and Efficiency:** Sonic delivers exceptional performance with:

*   10,000 Transactions per Second
*   Sub-Second Finality
*   Low Transaction Costs
*   Full EVM Compatibility

**Strong Security and Ethereum Compatibility:** Sonic maintains robust security through its aBFT (asynchronous Byzantine Fault Tolerance) consensus while offering full EVM compatibility. This allows developers to easily port their Ethereum applications to Sonic or build new ones using familiar tools and languages. **Developer-Friendly Environment:** Sonic provides developers with powerful incentives and infrastructure including:

*   Fee Monetization: Earn up to 90% of the fees your apps generate
*   Innovator Fund: Up to 200 million S to support new ventures
*   Solidity/Vyper Support
*   Comprehensive development tooling

[Sonic documentation\
-------------------\
\
Access comprehensive documentation for Sonic, providing detailed insights into its consensus mechanism, architecture, and development resources.](https://docs.soniclabs.com/sonic/overview)

[​](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/sonic/overview#data-catalog)

Data Catalog
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[Logs\
----\
\
Detailed event logs from smart contracts, offering insights into contract interactions and network activities on Sonic.](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/sonic/raw/logs)
[Blocks\
------\
\
Information on blocks processed through Sonic’s Lachesis consensus, demonstrating the network’s high throughput and fast finality.](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/sonic/raw/blocks)
[Transactions\
------------\
\
Extensive transaction data, showcasing the high-performance and cost-effective nature of operations on Sonic.](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/sonic/raw/transactions)
[decoded\
-------\
\
Decoded transaction data for easier analysis and deeper understanding of smart contract executions on the Sonic network.](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/sonic/decoded/overview)

# sonic.blocks - Dune Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/sonic/raw/blocks#content-area)

[Dune Docs home page![light logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo/logo/dune-logo-light.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo&q=85&s=8344ffbb623f6875145727e13925a620)![dark logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo/logo/dune-logo-dark.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo&q=85&s=54f1a9a73ae8fe5ec0235a2e52f9b870)](https://dune.com/)

Search...

⌘KAsk AI

Search...

Navigation

Raw

sonic.blocks

[Docs](https://docs.dune.com/home)
[Data Catalog](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/overview)
[API Reference](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction)
[SQL Query Engine](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/overview)
[Resources](https://docs.dune.com/resources/credits-billing/overview)

Table description
-----------------

The `sonic.blocks` table contains information about blocks in the sonic blockchain. A block is a collection of transactions that are hashed and added to the blockchain. Each block contains a reference to the previous block, known as the parent hash, and a timestamp. The table contains information about each block, such as the block number, the block hash, the block size, the number of transactions, and the gas used.

Column Descriptions
-------------------

Datatypes on Snowflake datashare are different in some cases, read more [here](https://docs.dune.com/datashare/datashare#datatypes)
.

Table Sample
------------

Examples
--------

### Show the most recent blocks

    SELECT
        number,
        hash, 
        size,
        gas_used
      FROM sonic.blocks
      ORDER BY number DESC
      LIMIT 10

### Show the number of blocks mined each day

    SELECT
        date_trunc('day', time) AS day,
        count(distinct number)
      FROM sonic.blocks
      GROUP BY day
      ORDER BY day DESC

### Show the number of transactions in each block

    SELECT
        number,
        count(*)
      FROM sonic.blocks
      GROUP BY 1 
      LIMIT 10

Sophon

Sophon Overview

[Docs](https://docs.dune.com/home)
[Data Catalog](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/overview)
[API Reference](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction)
[SQL Query Engine](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/overview)
[Resources](https://docs.dune.com/resources/credits-billing/overview)

On this page

*   [Data Catalog](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/sophon/overview#data-catalog)
    

Sophon is a ZK chain that redefines onchain experiences by combining real applications with a simple user experience and high scalability. Built on ZK technology, Sophon aims to bring crypto accessibility to a wider audience while maintaining robust security and performance. **Architecture and Technology:** Sophon is built on three key technological pillars:

*   **Validiums**: A ZK-based scaling solution that provides high throughput and security
*   **The ZK Stack**: A comprehensive infrastructure that powers the network
*   **Native Account Abstraction**: Built-in support for smart accounts and improved user experience
*   **Paymasters**: Advanced fee abstraction mechanisms for better user onboarding

**Enhanced User Experience:** Sophon focuses on simplifying the blockchain experience while maintaining high performance. The platform is designed to make crypto applications accessible to everyday users while providing the tools and infrastructure developers need to build sophisticated applications. **Developer-Centric Approach:** The platform provides a comprehensive environment for developers to build and deploy applications, with native support for advanced features like account abstraction and paymaster functionality, enabling more sophisticated and user-friendly dApps.

[Sophon documentation\
--------------------\
\
Access the official documentation for Sophon to explore its architecture, features, and development resources.](https://docs.sophon.xyz/welcome)

[​](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/sophon/overview#data-catalog)

Data Catalog
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[Logs\
----\
\
Event logs from smart contracts, providing insights into interactions and activities on the Sophon network.](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/sophon/raw/logs)
[Blocks\
------\
\
Information on blocks processed using Sophon’s ZK technology, reflecting the network’s capacity for high transaction throughput.](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/sophon/raw/blocks)
[Transactions\
------------\
\
Detailed transaction data, showcasing the operational efficiency and cost-effectiveness of Sophon’s validium solution.](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/sophon/raw/transactions)
[decoded\
-------\
\
Decoded transaction data for easier analysis and better understanding of smart contract executions on Sophon.](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/sophon/decoded/overview)

# sonic.logs - Dune Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/sonic/raw/logs#content-area)

[Dune Docs home page![light logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo/logo/dune-logo-light.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo&q=85&s=8344ffbb623f6875145727e13925a620)![dark logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo/logo/dune-logo-dark.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo&q=85&s=54f1a9a73ae8fe5ec0235a2e52f9b870)](https://dune.com/)

Search...

⌘KAsk AI

Search...

Navigation

Raw

sonic.logs

[Docs](https://docs.dune.com/home)
[Data Catalog](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/overview)
[API Reference](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction)
[SQL Query Engine](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/overview)
[Resources](https://docs.dune.com/resources/credits-billing/overview)

Table Description
-----------------

The `sonic.logs` table represents the logs generated by the Ethereum Virtual Machine (EVM) when a contract is executed. Logs are a way to store data on the blockchain. Logs originate from events that occur during the execution of a smart contract. A log consists of:

*   topic list: a list of 0 to 3 32-byte data topics. `Topic0` is the hash of the signature of the event (indexed), and the remaining topics are indexed parameters of the event.
*   data: contains non-indexed data.

This is the raw version of this table. If the chain is a Fully Managed chain, decoded transaction calls will be available, see [call tables](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/sonic/decoded/call-tables)
 section. If this is a Hosted chain, decoded call tables will not be available.

Column Descriptions
-------------------

Datatypes on Snowflake datashare are different in some cases, read more [here](https://docs.dune.com/datashare/datashare#datatypes)
.

Table Sample
------------

Examples
--------

### Filter the logs for a specific contract

    SELECT *
    FROM sonic.logs
    WHERE contract_address = 0x06012c8cf97bead5deae237070f9587f8e7a266d
    LIMIT 10

### Filter the logs for a specific topic

    SELECT *
    FROM sonic.logs
    WHERE topic0 = 0xddf252ad1be2c89b69c2b068fc378daa952ba7f163c4a11628f55a4df523b3ef
    

### Show the logs of a specific block

    SELECT *
    FROM sonic.logs
    WHERE evt_block_number = 1000000

Decoded

sophon.traces\_decoded

[Docs](https://docs.dune.com/home)
[Data Catalog](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/overview)
[API Reference](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction)
[SQL Query Engine](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/overview)
[Resources](https://docs.dune.com/resources/credits-billing/overview)

Table Description
-----------------

The `traces_decoded` table contains decoded traces from sophon transactions. The table matches `MethodID`, which consists of the first 4 bytes of any eth call, to the trace signature and the corresponding Method name. The table does not contain the full trace data and is not suitable for analysis of smart contract level data. For that, use the specific event tables as described in [Call-tables](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/sophon/decoded/traces-decoded)
.This table is great for gaining a high level understanding of the types of events that are being emitted by a smart contract or smart contracts of a certain protocol.

Column Descriptions
-------------------

Datatypes on Snowflake datashare are different in some cases, read more [here](https://docs.dune.com/datashare/datashare#datatypes)
.

Table Sample
------------

sophon.blocks

Table description
-----------------

The `sophon.blocks` table contains information about blocks in the sophon blockchain. A block is a collection of transactions that are hashed and added to the blockchain. Each block contains a reference to the previous block, known as the parent hash, and a timestamp. The table contains information about each block, such as the block number, the block hash, the block size, the number of transactions, and the gas used.

Column Descriptions
-------------------

Datatypes on Snowflake datashare are different in some cases, read more [here](https://docs.dune.com/datashare/datashare#datatypes)
.

Table Sample
------------

Examples
--------

### Show the most recent blocks

    SELECT
        number,
        hash, 
        size,
        gas_used
      FROM sophon.blocks
      ORDER BY number DESC
      LIMIT 10

### Show the number of blocks mined each day

    SELECT
        date_trunc('day', time) AS day,
        count(distinct number)
      FROM sophon.blocks
      GROUP BY day
      ORDER BY day DESC

### Show the number of transactions in each block

    SELECT
        number,
        count(*)
      FROM sophon.blocks
      GROUP BY 1 
      LIMIT 10

# Sonic Call Tables - Dune Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/sonic/decoded/call-tables#content-area)

[Dune Docs home page![light logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo/logo/dune-logo-light.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo&q=85&s=8344ffbb623f6875145727e13925a620)![dark logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo/logo/dune-logo-dark.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo&q=85&s=54f1a9a73ae8fe5ec0235a2e52f9b870)](https://dune.com/)

Search...

⌘KAsk AI

Search...

Navigation

Decoded

Sonic Call Tables

[Docs](https://docs.dune.com/home)
[Data Catalog](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/overview)
[API Reference](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction)
[SQL Query Engine](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/overview)
[Resources](https://docs.dune.com/resources/credits-billing/overview)

On this page

*   [Overview](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/sonic/decoded/call-tables#overview)
    
*   [Decoding](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/sonic/decoded/call-tables#decoding)
    
*   [Multiple Instances](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/sonic/decoded/call-tables#multiple-instances)
    
*   [Common misconceptions](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/sonic/decoded/call-tables#common-misconceptions)
    
*   [Further Reading](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/sonic/decoded/call-tables#further-reading)
    

[​](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/sonic/decoded/call-tables#overview)

Overview
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

On Dune, we parse all message calls and transactions made to smart contracts in their own tables. This allows us to isolate the logic of a specific smart contract and analyze how it interacts with other smart contracts. The data is stored in the format: `[projectname_blockchain].[contractName]_call_[functionName]` This allows us to analyze how a specific function is used in a smart contract, and how often it is called, as well as how it interacts with other smart contracts. Call tables always originate from the `traces` table, which contains all the transactions and message calls on the Ethereum network. We parse the `data` field of the `traces` table to decode the function call and parameters.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/sonic/decoded/call-tables#decoding)

Decoding
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

When a transaction is sent to a smart contract on the Ethereum network, it contains a `data` field. This `data` field is the encoded function call and parameters. Dune decodes this data and stores it in the corresponding table. For example, when a transaction is sent to the [Uniswap v3 factory](https://etherscan.io/address/0x1f98431c8ad98523631ae4a59f267346ea31f984#code)
 contract on the Ethereum network, Dune will decode the `data` field and store it in the table: `uniswap_v3_ethereum.Factory_call_createPool`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/sonic/decoded/call-tables#multiple-instances)

Multiple Instances
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

For a contract where multiple instances exist, we will decode all calls to all instances of this smart contract into one table. If there are transactions calling the `swap` function of any instance of the [Uniswap v3 pair](https://etherscan.io/address/0x8f8ef111b67c04eb1641f5ff19ee54cda062f163#writeContract)
 contract, we will decode this data into the table `uniswap_v3_ethereum.Pair_call_swap`. The `pair` contract is a template contract and there are many instances of it, each with its own address. The column `contract_address` will indicate the address of the instance of the pair contract that was called.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/sonic/decoded/call-tables#common-misconceptions)

Common misconceptions
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

One thing to keep in mind here is that [web3.js](https://web3js.readthedocs.io/)
, [web3.py](https://web3py.readthedocs.io/en/stable)
 and all other methods of (locally) calling a `pure`, `read`, or `constant` function do not broadcast or publish anything on the blockchain and are therefore not recorded in Dune. However, if one of these functions is invoked by another smart contract in the context of a transaction, this will be broadcast on the chain and therefore accessible in Dune. In short: **State data stored in the memory of a smart contract is not available on Dune!** A good example of this is the function `decimals` of the [erc20 token contract](https://etherscan.io/token/0x1f9840a85d5af5bf1d1762f925bdaddc4201f984#readContract)
 `Uni` which is a `constant` state variable that is able to be accessed through an automatically created “[getter function](https://docs.soliditylang.org/en/v0.7.4/contracts.html#getter-functions)
”. Should a smart contract invoke this function in the context of transaction, this message call will be recorded in the Dune table [`uniswap."UNI_call_decimals"`](https://dune.com/queries/741354)
. This is in contrast to anyone calling this function locally using web3.py/web3.js or using the Etherscan frontend to access this state. These local calls are not recorded in Dune.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/sonic/decoded/call-tables#further-reading)

Further Reading
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[What is the difference between a transaction and a call?\
--------------------------------------------------------](https://ethereum.stackexchange.com/questions/765/what-is-the-difference-between-a-transaction-and-a-call)
[Soliditylang.org documentation\
------------------------------](https://docs.soliditylang.org/en/v0.8.13/contracts.html#function-visibility)
[How Calldata is Encoded\
-----------------------](https://degatchi.com/articles/reading-raw-evm-calldata)

[Sonic Decoded Overview](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/sonic/decoded/overview)

⌘I

# sonic.traces - Dune Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/sonic/raw/traces#content-area)

[Dune Docs home page![light logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo/logo/dune-logo-light.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo&q=85&s=8344ffbb623f6875145727e13925a620)![dark logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo/logo/dune-logo-dark.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo&q=85&s=54f1a9a73ae8fe5ec0235a2e52f9b870)](https://dune.com/)

Raw

sonic.traces

[Docs](https://docs.dune.com/home)
[Data Catalog](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/overview)
[API Reference](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction)
[SQL Query Engine](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/overview)
[Resources](https://docs.dune.com/resources/credits-billing/overview)

Table Description
-----------------

The `sonic.traces` table contains the traces of the transactions executed on the Ethereum Virtual Machine (EVM). It includes the traces of the transaction and the traces of the internal transactions. Traces are the result of the execution of the transaction and are used to debug and understand the execution of the transaction. They are also known as \`internal transactions\` and can be used to understand the execution of a transaction.

This is the raw version of this table. If the chain is a Fully Managed chain, decoded transaction calls will be available, see [call tables](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/sonic/decoded/call-tables)
 section. If this is a Hosted chain, decoded call tables will not be available.

Column Descriptions
-------------------

Datatypes on Snowflake datashare are different in some cases, read more [here](https://docs.dune.com/datashare/datashare#datatypes)
.

Table Sample
------------

Example
-------

### Querying traces for a specific transaction hash

    SELECT *
    FROM sonic.traces
    WHERE tx_hash = 0xb30d6d67cf7d148c2257bf598c5f5cdf5912a3d05c7d3b000398d675d2fa912c

# Sophon Call Tables - Dune Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/sophon/decoded/call-tables#content-area)

[Dune Docs home page![light logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo/logo/dune-logo-light.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo&q=85&s=8344ffbb623f6875145727e13925a620)![dark logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo/logo/dune-logo-dark.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo&q=85&s=54f1a9a73ae8fe5ec0235a2e52f9b870)](https://dune.com/)

Decoded

Sophon Call Tables

[Docs](https://docs.dune.com/home)
[Data Catalog](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/overview)
[API Reference](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction)
[SQL Query Engine](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/overview)
[Resources](https://docs.dune.com/resources/credits-billing/overview)

On this page

*   [Overview](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/sophon/decoded/call-tables#overview)
    
*   [Decoding](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/sophon/decoded/call-tables#decoding)
    
*   [Multiple Instances](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/sophon/decoded/call-tables#multiple-instances)
    
*   [Common misconceptions](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/sophon/decoded/call-tables#common-misconceptions)
    
*   [Further Reading](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/sophon/decoded/call-tables#further-reading)
    

[​](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/sophon/decoded/call-tables#overview)

Overview
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

On Dune, we parse all message calls and transactions made to smart contracts in their own tables. This allows us to isolate the logic of a specific smart contract and analyze how it interacts with other smart contracts. The data is stored in the format: `[projectname_blockchain].[contractName]_call_[functionName]` This allows us to analyze how a specific function is used in a smart contract, and how often it is called, as well as how it interacts with other smart contracts. Call tables always originate from the `traces` table, which contains all the transactions and message calls on the Ethereum network. We parse the `data` field of the `traces` table to decode the function call and parameters.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/sophon/decoded/call-tables#decoding)

Decoding
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

When a transaction is sent to a smart contract on the Ethereum network, it contains a `data` field. This `data` field is the encoded function call and parameters. Dune decodes this data and stores it in the corresponding table. For example, when a transaction is sent to the [Uniswap v3 factory](https://etherscan.io/address/0x1f98431c8ad98523631ae4a59f267346ea31f984#code)
 contract on the Ethereum network, Dune will decode the `data` field and store it in the table: `uniswap_v3_ethereum.Factory_call_createPool`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/sophon/decoded/call-tables#multiple-instances)

Multiple Instances
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

For a contract where multiple instances exist, we will decode all calls to all instances of this smart contract into one table. If there are transactions calling the `swap` function of any instance of the [Uniswap v3 pair](https://etherscan.io/address/0x8f8ef111b67c04eb1641f5ff19ee54cda062f163#writeContract)
 contract, we will decode this data into the table `uniswap_v3_ethereum.Pair_call_swap`. The `pair` contract is a template contract and there are many instances of it, each with its own address. The column `contract_address` will indicate the address of the instance of the pair contract that was called.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/sophon/decoded/call-tables#common-misconceptions)

Common misconceptions
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

One thing to keep in mind here is that [web3.js](https://web3js.readthedocs.io/)
, [web3.py](https://web3py.readthedocs.io/en/stable)
 and all other methods of (locally) calling a `pure`, `read`, or `constant` function do not broadcast or publish anything on the blockchain and are therefore not recorded in Dune. However, if one of these functions is invoked by another smart contract in the context of a transaction, this will be broadcast on the chain and therefore accessible in Dune. In short: **State data stored in the memory of a smart contract is not available on Dune!** A good example of this is the function `decimals` of the [erc20 token contract](https://etherscan.io/token/0x1f9840a85d5af5bf1d1762f925bdaddc4201f984#readContract)
 `Uni` which is a `constant` state variable that is able to be accessed through an automatically created “[getter function](https://docs.soliditylang.org/en/v0.7.4/contracts.html#getter-functions)
”. Should a smart contract invoke this function in the context of transaction, this message call will be recorded in the Dune table [`uniswap."UNI_call_decimals"`](https://dune.com/queries/741354)
. This is in contrast to anyone calling this function locally using web3.py/web3.js or using the Etherscan frontend to access this state. These local calls are not recorded in Dune.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/sophon/decoded/call-tables#further-reading)

Further Reading
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

[What is the difference between a transaction and a call?\
--------------------------------------------------------](https://ethereum.stackexchange.com/questions/765/what-is-the-difference-between-a-transaction-and-a-call)
[Soliditylang.org documentation\
------------------------------](https://docs.soliditylang.org/en/v0.8.13/contracts.html#function-visibility)
[How Calldata is Encoded\
-----------------------](https://degatchi.com/articles/reading-raw-evm-calldata)

# sonic.transactions - Dune Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/sonic/raw/transactions#content-area)

[Dune Docs home page![light logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo/logo/dune-logo-light.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo&q=85&s=8344ffbb623f6875145727e13925a620)![dark logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo/logo/dune-logo-dark.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo&q=85&s=54f1a9a73ae8fe5ec0235a2e52f9b870)](https://dune.com/)

Search...

⌘KAsk AI

Search...

Navigation

Raw

sonic.transactions

[Docs](https://docs.dune.com/home)
[Data Catalog](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/overview)
[API Reference](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction)
[SQL Query Engine](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/overview)
[Resources](https://docs.dune.com/resources/credits-billing/overview)

Table Description
-----------------

The `sonic.transactions` table contains information about all transactions on the sonic blockchain. Each row represents a single transaction and includes information such as block number, hash, timestamp, sender, recipient, value, gas, gas price, and more. Transactions are the fundamental unit of interaction with the sonic blockchain. Transactions are created by users and are used to send value, deploy smart contracts, and interact with smart contracts.

This is the raw version of this table. If the chain is a Fully Managed chain, decoded transaction calls will be available, see [call tables](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/sonic/decoded/call-tables)
 section. If this is a Hosted chain, decoded call tables will not be available.

Column Descriptions
-------------------

Datatypes on Snowflake datashare are different in some cases, read more [here](https://docs.dune.com/datashare/datashare#datatypes)
.

Table Sample
------------

Examples
--------

### Show all transactions sent by a specific address

    SELECT * 
    FROM sonic.transactions WHERE "from" = '0x50A1b5c358F8D34F0d35aA2f10742c46054E247e'
    

### Count the number of transactions per block

    SELECT 
        block_number, 
        COUNT(*)
    FROM sonic.transactions
    GROUP BY 1
    ORDER BY 1 DESC
    LIMIT 10
    

### Show the top 10 transactions with the highest gas price

    SELECT 
        hash, 
        gas_price
    FROM sonic.transactions
    ORDER BY gas_price DESC
    LIMIT 10

# sophon.logs_decoded - Dune Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/sophon/decoded/logs-decoded#content-area)

[Dune Docs home page![light logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo/logo/dune-logo-light.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo&q=85&s=8344ffbb623f6875145727e13925a620)![dark logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo/logo/dune-logo-dark.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo&q=85&s=54f1a9a73ae8fe5ec0235a2e52f9b870)](https://dune.com/)

Decoded

sophon.logs\_decoded

[Docs](https://docs.dune.com/home)
[Data Catalog](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/overview)
[API Reference](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction)
[SQL Query Engine](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/overview)
[Resources](https://docs.dune.com/resources/credits-billing/overview)

Table Description
-----------------

The `logs_decoded` table contains decoded logs from sophon transactions. The table matches `topic0` to the event signature and the corresponding event name. The table does not contain the full event data and is not suitable for analysis of smart contract level data. For that, use the specific event tables as described in [Event Logs](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/sophon/decoded/event-logs)
.This table is great for gaining a high level understanding of the types of events that are being emitted by a smart contract or smart contracts of a certain protocol.

Column Descriptions
-------------------

Datatypes on Snowflake datashare are different in some cases, read more [here](https://docs.dune.com/datashare/datashare#datatypes)
.

Table Sample
------------

# sophon.logs - Dune Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/sophon/raw/logs#content-area)

[Dune Docs home page![light logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo/logo/dune-logo-light.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo&q=85&s=8344ffbb623f6875145727e13925a620)![dark logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo/logo/dune-logo-dark.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo&q=85&s=54f1a9a73ae8fe5ec0235a2e52f9b870)](https://dune.com/)

Search...

⌘KAsk AI

Search...

Navigation

Raw

sophon.logs

[Docs](https://docs.dune.com/home)
[Data Catalog](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/overview)
[API Reference](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction)
[SQL Query Engine](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/overview)
[Resources](https://docs.dune.com/resources/credits-billing/overview)

Table Description
-----------------

The `sophon.logs` table represents the logs generated by the Ethereum Virtual Machine (EVM) when a contract is executed. Logs are a way to store data on the blockchain. Logs originate from events that occur during the execution of a smart contract. A log consists of:

*   topic list: a list of 0 to 3 32-byte data topics. `Topic0` is the hash of the signature of the event (indexed), and the remaining topics are indexed parameters of the event.
*   data: contains non-indexed data.

This is the raw version of this table. If the chain is a Fully Managed chain, decoded transaction calls will be available, see [call tables](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/sophon/decoded/call-tables)
 section. If this is a Hosted chain, decoded call tables will not be available.

Column Descriptions
-------------------

Datatypes on Snowflake datashare are different in some cases, read more [here](https://docs.dune.com/datashare/datashare#datatypes)
.

Table Sample
------------

Examples
--------

### Filter the logs for a specific contract

    SELECT *
    FROM sophon.logs
    WHERE contract_address = 0x06012c8cf97bead5deae237070f9587f8e7a266d
    LIMIT 10

### Filter the logs for a specific topic

    SELECT *
    FROM sophon.logs
    WHERE topic0 = 0xddf252ad1be2c89b69c2b068fc378daa952ba7f163c4a11628f55a4df523b3ef
    

### Show the logs of a specific block

    SELECT *
    FROM sophon.logs
    WHERE evt_block_number = 1000000

# sonic.creation_traces - Dune Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/sonic/raw/creation-traces#content-area)

[Dune Docs home page![light logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo/logo/dune-logo-light.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo&q=85&s=8344ffbb623f6875145727e13925a620)![dark logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo/logo/dune-logo-dark.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo&q=85&s=54f1a9a73ae8fe5ec0235a2e52f9b870)](https://dune.com/)

Search...

⌘KAsk AI

Search...

Navigation

Raw

sonic.creation\_traces

[Docs](https://docs.dune.com/home)
[Data Catalog](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/overview)
[API Reference](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction)
[SQL Query Engine](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/overview)
[Resources](https://docs.dune.com/resources/credits-billing/overview)

Table Description
-----------------

The `sonic.creation_traces` table contains information about the creation of smart contracts on the sonic blockchain. This includes the address of the contract, the address of the creator, the block number at which the contract was created, the transaction hash, and the contract's bytecode. This table is useful for understanding the deployment of smart contracts on the sonic blockchain.

This table is a subset of the `traces` table, which contains information about all traces on the sonic blockchain. The `creation_traces` table is filtered to only include traces that create new smart contracts. The filter for this is `type = 'create'` .

Column Descriptions
-------------------

Datatypes on Snowflake datashare are different in some cases, read more [here](https://docs.dune.com/datashare/datashare#datatypes)
.

Table Sample
------------

Examples
--------

### Show the creation of a specific smart contract

    SELECT * FROM sonic.creation_traces
    WHERE contract_address = 0x06012c8cf97bead5deae237070f9587f8e7a266d

### Show the creation of smart contracts by a specific creator

    SELECT * FROM sonic.creation_traces
    WHERE "from" = 0x0d4a11d5eeaac28ec3f61d100da81f6a1b65c9d6

### Show the creation of smart contracts in the last 10 days

    SELECT 
        date_trunc('day', block_time) AS day,
        COUNT(*)
    FROM sonic.creation_traces
    GROUP BY 1
    ORDER BY 1 DESC
    LIMIT 10

# Event Logs - Dune Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/sophon/decoded/event-logs#content-area)

[Dune Docs home page![light logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo/logo/dune-logo-light.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo&q=85&s=8344ffbb623f6875145727e13925a620)![dark logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo/logo/dune-logo-dark.svg?fit=max&auto=format&n=2zcFQ4cOAgHOUIIo&q=85&s=54f1a9a73ae8fe5ec0235a2e52f9b870)](https://dune.com/)
